andre@comecandocomlinux:~$ help cd
cd: cd [-L|[-P [-e]] [-@]] [dir]
    Change the shell working directory.
    
    Change the current directory to DIR.  The default DIR is the value of the
    HOME shell variable.
    
    The variable CDPATH defines the search path for the directory containing
    DIR.  Alternative directory names in CDPATH are separated by a colon (:).
    A null directory name is the same as the current directory.  If DIR begins
    with a slash (/), then CDPATH is not used.
    
    If the directory is not found, and the shell option `cdable_vars' is set,
    the word is assumed to be  a variable name.  If that variable has a value,
    its value is used for DIR.
    
    Options:
      -L	force symbolic links to be followed: resolve symbolic
    		links in DIR after processing instances of `..'
      -P	use the physical directory structure without following
    		symbolic links: resolve symbolic links in DIR before
    		processing instances of `..'
      -e	if the -P option is supplied, and the current working
    		directory cannot be determined successfully, exit with
    		a non-zero status
      -@	on systems that support it, present a file with extended
    		attributes as a directory containing the file attributes
    
    The default is to follow symbolic links, as if `-L' were specified.
    `..' is processed by removing the immediately previous pathname component
    back to a slash or the beginning of DIR.
    
    Exit Status:
    Returns 0 if the directory is changed, and if $PWD is set successfully when
    -P is used; non-zero otherwise.
andre@comecandocomlinux:~$ ls -he[K[K-help
Usage: ls [OPTION]... [FILE]...
List information about the FILEs (the current directory by default).
Sort entries alphabetically if none of -cftuvSUX nor --sort is specified.

Mandatory arguments to long options are mandatory for short options too.
  -a, --all                  do not ignore entries starting with .
  -A, --almost-all           do not list implied . and ..
      --author               with -l, print the author of each file
  -b, --escape               print C-style escapes for nongraphic characters
      --block-size=SIZE      scale sizes by SIZE before printing them; e.g.,
                               '--block-size=M' prints sizes in units of
                               1,048,576 bytes; see SIZE format below
  -B, --ignore-backups       do not list implied entries ending with ~
  -c                         with -lt: sort by, and show, ctime (time of last
                               modification of file status information);
                               with -l: show ctime and sort by name;
                               otherwise: sort by ctime, newest first
  -C                         list entries by columns
      --color[=WHEN]         colorize the output; WHEN can be 'always' (default
                               if omitted), 'auto', or 'never'; more info below
  -d, --directory            list directories themselves, not their contents
  -D, --dired                generate output designed for Emacs' dired mode
  -f                         do not sort, enable -aU, disable -ls --color
  -F, --classify             append indicator (one of */=>@|) to entries
      --file-type            likewise, except do not append '*'
      --format=WORD          across -x, commas -m, horizontal -x, long -l,
                               single-column -1, verbose -l, vertical -C
      --full-time            like -l --time-style=full-iso
  -g                         like -l, but do not list owner
      --group-directories-first
                             group directories before files;
                               can be augmented with a --sort option, but any
                               use of --sort=none (-U) disables grouping
  -G, --no-group             in a long listing, don't print group names
  -h, --human-readable       with -l and/or -s, print human readable sizes
                               (e.g., 1K 234M 2G)
      --si                   likewise, but use powers of 1000 not 1024
  -H, --dereference-command-line
                             follow symbolic links listed on the command line
      --dereference-command-line-symlink-to-dir
                             follow each command line symbolic link
                               that points to a directory
      --hide=PATTERN         do not list implied entries matching shell PATTERN
                               (overridden by -a or -A)
      --hyperlink[=WHEN]     hyperlink file names; WHEN can be 'always'
                               (default if omitted), 'auto', or 'never'
      --indicator-style=WORD  append indicator with style WORD to entry names:
                               none (default), slash (-p),
                               file-type (--file-type), classify (-F)
  -i, --inode                print the index number of each file
  -I, --ignore=PATTERN       do not list implied entries matching shell PATTERN
  -k, --kibibytes            default to 1024-byte blocks for disk usage
  -l                         use a long listing format
  -L, --dereference          when showing file information for a symbolic
                               link, show information for the file the link
                               references rather than for the link itself
  -m                         fill width with a comma separated list of entries
  -n, --numeric-uid-gid      like -l, but list numeric user and group IDs
  -N, --literal              print entry names without quoting
  -o                         like -l, but do not list group information
  -p, --indicator-style=slash
                             append / indicator to directories
  -q, --hide-control-chars   print ? instead of nongraphic characters
      --show-control-chars   show nongraphic characters as-is (the default,
                               unless program is 'ls' and output is a terminal)
  -Q, --quote-name           enclose entry names in double quotes
      --quoting-style=WORD   use quoting style WORD for entry names:
                               literal, locale, shell, shell-always,
                               shell-escape, shell-escape-always, c, escape
  -r, --reverse              reverse order while sorting
  -R, --recursive            list subdirectories recursively
  -s, --size                 print the allocated size of each file, in blocks
  -S                         sort by file size, largest first
      --sort=WORD            sort by WORD instead of name: none (-U), size (-S),
                               time (-t), version (-v), extension (-X)
      --time=WORD            with -l, show time as WORD instead of default
                               modification time: atime or access or use (-u);
                               ctime or status (-c); also use specified time
                               as sort key if --sort=time (newest first)
      --time-style=STYLE     with -l, show times using style STYLE:
                               full-iso, long-iso, iso, locale, or +FORMAT;
                               FORMAT is interpreted like in 'date'; if FORMAT
                               is FORMAT1<newline>FORMAT2, then FORMAT1 applies
                               to non-recent files and FORMAT2 to recent files;
                               if STYLE is prefixed with 'posix-', STYLE
                               takes effect only outside the POSIX locale
  -t                         sort by modification time, newest first
  -T, --tabsize=COLS         assume tab stops at each COLS instead of 8
  -u                         with -lt: sort by, and show, access time;
                               with -l: show access time and sort by name;
                               otherwise: sort by access time, newest first
  -U                         do not sort; list entries in directory order
  -v                         natural sort of (version) numbers within text
  -w, --width=COLS           set output width to COLS.  0 means no limit
  -x                         list entries by lines instead of by columns
  -X                         sort alphabetically by entry extension
  -Z, --context              print any security context of each file
  -1                         list one file per line.  Avoid '\n' with -q or -b
      --help     display this help and exit
      --version  output version information and exit

The SIZE argument is an integer and optional unit (example: 10K is 10*1024).
Units are K,M,G,T,P,E,Z,Y (powers of 1024) or KB,MB,... (powers of 1000).

Using color to distinguish file types is disabled both by default and
with --color=never.  With --color=auto, ls emits color codes only when
standard output is connected to a terminal.  The LS_COLORS environment
variable can change the settings.  Use the dircolors command to set it.

Exit status:
 0  if OK,
 1  if minor problems (e.g., cannot access subdirectory),
 2  if serious trouble (e.g., cannot access command-line argument).

GNU coreutils online help: <http://www.gnu.org/software/coreutils/>
Full documentation at: <http://www.gnu.org/software/coreutils/ls>
or available locally via: info '(coreutils) ls invocation'

FIND(1)                              General Commands Manual                              FIND(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[m[m
       find - search for files in a directory hierarchy[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[m[m
       [1mfind[m [-H] [-L] [-P] [-D debugopts] [-Olevel] [starting-point...] [expression][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[m[m
       This  manual page documents the GNU version of [1mfind[m.  GNU [1mfind[m searches the directory tree[m
       rooted at each given starting-point by evaluating the given expression from left to right,[m
       according  to  the rules of precedence (see section OPERATORS), until the outcome is known[m
       (the left hand side is false for [4mand[24m operations, true for [4mor[24m), at which point  [1mfind[m  moves[m
       on to the next file name.  If no starting-point is specified, `.' is assumed.[m
[m
       If  you  are  using [1mfind[m in an environment where security is important (for example if you[m
       are using it to search directories that are writable by other users), you should read  the[m
       `Security  Considerations' chapter of the findutils documentation, which is called [1mFinding[m[m
       [1mFiles[m and comes with findutils.   That document also includes a lot more detail  and  disโ[m
       cussion than this manual page, so you may find it a more useful source of information.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[m[m
       The [1m-H[m, [1m-L[m and [1m-P[m options control the treatment of symbolic links.  Command-line arguments[m
       following these are taken to be names of files or directories to be examined,  up  to  the[m
       first  argument  that  begins with `-', or the argument `(' or `!'.  That argument and any[m
       following arguments are taken to be the expression describing what is to be searched  for.[m
       If  no  paths  are  given,  the current directory is used.  If no expression is given, the[m
       expression [1m-print[m is used (but you should probably consider using  [1m-print0[m  instead,  anyโ[m
       way).[m
[m
       This  manual page talks about `options' within the expression list.  These options control[m
       the behaviour of [1mfind[m but are specified immediately after the last path  name.   The  five[m
       `real' options [1m-H[m, [1m-L[m, [1m-P[m, [1m-D[m and [1m-O[m must appear before the first path name, if at all.  A[m
       double dash [1m--[m can also be used to signal that any remaining  arguments  are  not  options[m
       (though ensuring that all start points begin with either `./' or `/' is generally safer if[m
       you use wildcards in the list of start points).[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 2 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K       -P     Never follow symbolic links.  This is the default behaviour.  When [1mfind[m examines or[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 3 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              prints  information  a  file, and the file is a symbolic link, the information used[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 4 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              shall be taken from the properties of the symbolic link itself.[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 5 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 6 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K       -L     Follow symbolic links.  When [1mfind[m examines or prints information about  files,  the[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 7 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              information  used  shall be taken from the properties of the file to which the link[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 8 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              points, not from the link itself (unless it is a broken symbolic link  or  [1mfind[m  is[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 9 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              unable  to  examine the file to which the link points).  Use of this option implies[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 10 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              [1m-noleaf[m.  If you later use the [1m-P[m option, [1m-noleaf[m will still be in effect.   If  [1m-L[m[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 11 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              is  in  effect  and  [1mfind[m  discovers  a  symbolic link to a subdirectory during its[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 12 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              search, the subdirectory pointed to by the symbolic link will be searched.[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 13 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 14 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              When the [1m-L[m option is in effect, the [1m-type[m predicate will always match against  the[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 15 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              type of the file that a symbolic link points to rather than the link itself (unless[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 16 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              the symbolic link is broken).  Actions that can cause symbolic links to become broโ[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 17 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              ken while [1mfind[m is executing (for example [1m-delete[m) can give rise to confusing behavโ[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 18 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              iour.  Using [1m-L[m causes the [1m-lname[m and [1m-ilname[m predicates always to return false.[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 19 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 20 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K       -H     Do not follow symbolic links, except while processing the command  line  arguments.[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 21 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              When [1mfind[m examines or prints information about files, the information used shall be[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 22 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              taken from the properties of the symbolic link itself.   The only exception to this[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 23 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              behaviour  is when a file specified on the command line is a symbolic link, and the[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 24 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              link can be resolved.  For that situation, the information used is taken from whatโ[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 25 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              ever the link points to (that is, the link is followed).  The information about the[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 26 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              link itself is used as a fallback if the file pointed to by the symbolic link  canโ[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 27 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              not  be examined.  If [1m-H[m is in effect and one of the paths specified on the command[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 28 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              line is a symbolic link to a directory, the contents  of  that  directory  will  be[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 29 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K              examined (though of course -maxdepth 0 would prevent this).[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 30 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 31 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K       If  more  than  one of [1m-H[m, [1m-L[m and [1m-P[m is specified, each overrides the others; the last one[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 32 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K       appearing on the command line takes effect.  Since it is the default, the [1m-P[m option should[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 33 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K       be considered to be in effect unless either [1m-H[m or [1m-L[m is specified.[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 34 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 35 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K       GNU  [1mfind[m  frequently stats files during the processing of the command line itself, before[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 36 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K       any searching has begun.  These options also affect how  those  arguments  are  processed.[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 37 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K       Specifically,  there  are  a number of tests that compare files listed on the command line[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 38 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[KBB[K       against a file we are currently considering.  In each case, the file specified on the comโ[m

andre@comecandocomlinux:~$ help cd
cd: cd [-L|[-P [-e]] [-@]] [dir]
    Change the shell working directory.
    
    Change the current directory to DIR.  The default DIR is the value of the
    HOME shell variable.
    
    The variable CDPATH defines the search path for the directory containing
    DIR.  Alternative directory names in CDPATH are separated by a colon (:).
    A null directory name is the same as the current directory.  If DIR begins
    with a slash (/), then CDPATH is not used.
    
    If the directory is not found, and the shell option `cdable_vars' is set,
    the word is assumed to be  a variable name.  If that variable has a value,
    its value is used for DIR.
    
    Options:
      -L	force symbolic links to be followed: resolve symbolic
    		links in DIR after processing instances of `..'
      -P	use the physical directory structure without following
    		symbolic links: resolve symbolic links in DIR before
    		processing instances of `..'
      -e	if the -P option is supplied, and the current working
    		directory cannot be determined successfully, exit with
    		a non-zero status
      -@	on systems that support it, present a file with extended
    		attributes as a directory containing the file attributes
    
    The default is to follow symbolic links, as if `-L' were specified.
    `..' is processed by removing the immediately previous pathname component
    back to a slash or the beginning of DIR.
[7m--More--[27m    [K
    Exit Status:
    Returns 0 if the directory is changed, and if $PWD is set successfully when
    -P is used; non-zero otherwise.
andre@comecandocomlinux:~$ ls -he[K[K-help
Usage: ls [OPTION]... [FILE]...
List information about the FILEs (the current directory by default).
Sort entries alphabetically if none of -cftuvSUX nor --sort is specified.

Mandatory arguments to long options are mandatory for short options too.
  -a, --all                  do not ignore entries starting with .
  -A, --almost-all           do not list implied . and ..
      --author               with -l, print the author of each file
  -b, --escape               print C-style escapes for nongraphic characters
      --block-size=SIZE      scale sizes by SIZE before printing them; e.g.,
                               '--block-size=M' prints sizes in units of
                               1,048,576 bytes; see SIZE format below
  -B, --ignore-backups       do not list implied entries ending with ~
  -c                         with -lt: sort by, and show, ctime (time of last
                               modification of file status information);
                               with -l: show ctime and sort by name;
                               otherwise: sort by ctime, newest first
  -C                         list entries by columns
      --color[=WHEN]         colorize the output; WHEN can be 'always' (default
                               if omitted), 'auto', or 'never'; more info below
  -d, --directory            list directories themselves, not their contents
  -D, --dired                generate output designed for Emacs' dired mode
  -f                         do not sort, enable -aU, disable -ls --color
  -F, --classify             append indicator (one of */=>@|) to entries
      --file-type            likewise, except do not append '*'
      --format=WORD          across -x, commas -m, horizontal -x, long -l,
                               single-column -1, verbose -l, vertical -C
      --full-time            like -l --time-style=full-iso
  -g                         like -l, but do not list owner
      --group-directories-first
                             group directories before files;
[7m--More--[27m                               can be augmented with a --sort option, but any
                               use of --sort=none (-U) disables grouping
  -G, --no-group             in a long listing, don't print group names
  -h, --human-readable       with -l and/or -s, print human readable sizes
                               (e.g., 1K 234M 2G)
      --si                   likewise, but use powers of 1000 not 1024
  -H, --dereference-command-line
                             follow symbolic links listed on the command line
      --dereference-command-line-symlink-to-dir
                             follow each command line symbolic link
                               that points to a directory
      --hide=PATTERN         do not list implied entries matching shell PATTERN
                               (overridden by -a or -A)
      --hyperlink[=WHEN]     hyperlink file names; WHEN can be 'always'
                               (default if omitted), 'auto', or 'never'
      --indicator-style=WORD  append indicator with style WORD to entry names:
                               none (default), slash (-p),
                               file-type (--file-type), classify (-F)
  -i, --inode                print the index number of each file
  -I, --ignore=PATTERN       do not list implied entries matching shell PATTERN
  -k, --kibibytes            default to 1024-byte blocks for disk usage
  -l                         use a long listing format
  -L, --dereference          when showing file information for a symbolic
                               link, show information for the file the link
                               references rather than for the link itself
  -m                         fill width with a comma separated list of entries
  -n, --numeric-uid-gid      like -l, but list numeric user and group IDs
  -N, --literal              print entry names without quoting
  -o                         like -l, but do not list group information
  -p, --indicator-style=slash
                             append / indicator to directories
  -q, --hide-control-chars   print ? instead of nongraphic characters
      --show-control-chars   show nongraphic characters as-is (the default,
                               unless program is 'ls' and output is a terminal)
  -Q, --quote-name           enclose entry names in double quotes
      --quoting-style=WORD   use quoting style WORD for entry names:
[7m--More--[27m                               literal, locale, shell, shell-always,
                               shell-escape, shell-escape-always, c, escape
  -r, --reverse              reverse order while sorting
  -R, --recursive            list subdirectories recursively
  -s, --size                 print the allocated size of each file, in blocks
  -S                         sort by file size, largest first
      --sort=WORD            sort by WORD instead of name: none (-U), size (-S),
                               time (-t), version (-v), extension (-X)
      --time=WORD            with -l, show time as WORD instead of default
                               modification time: atime or access or use (-u);
                               ctime or status (-c); also use specified time
                               as sort key if --sort=time (newest first)
      --time-style=STYLE     with -l, show times using style STYLE:
                               full-iso, long-iso, iso, locale, or +FORMAT;
                               FORMAT is interpreted like in 'date'; if FORMAT
                               is FORMAT1<newline>FORMAT2, then FORMAT1 applies
                               to non-recent files and FORMAT2 to recent files;
                               if STYLE is prefixed with 'posix-', STYLE
                               takes effect only outside the POSIX locale
  -t                         sort by modification time, newest first
  -T, --tabsize=COLS         assume tab stops at each COLS instead of 8
  -u                         with -lt: sort by, and show, access time;
                               with -l: show access time and sort by name;
                               otherwise: sort by access time, newest first
  -U                         do not sort; list entries in directory order
  -v                         natural sort of (version) numbers within text
  -w, --width=COLS           set output width to COLS.  0 means no limit
  -x                         list entries by lines instead of by columns
  -X                         sort alphabetically by entry extension
  -Z, --context              print any security context of each file
  -1                         list one file per line.  Avoid '\n' with -q or -b
      --help     display this help and exit
      --version  output version information and exit

The SIZE argument is an integer and optional unit (example: 10K is 10*1024).
Units are K,M,G,T,P,E,Z,Y (powers of 1024) or KB,MB,... (powers of 1000).
[7m--More--[27m[K
Using color to distinguish file types is disabled both by default and
with --color=never.  With --color=auto, ls emits color codes only when
standard output is connected to a terminal.  The LS_COLORS environment
variable can change the settings.  Use the dircolors command to set it.

Exit status:
 0  if OK,
 1  if minor problems (e.g., cannot access subdirectory),
 2  if serious trouble (e.g., cannot access command-line argument).

GNU coreutils online help: <http://www.gnu.org/software/coreutils/>
Full documentation at: <http://www.gnu.org/software/coreutils/ls>
or available locally via: info '(coreutils) ls invocation'

FIND(1)                              General Commands Manual                              FIND(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[m[m
       find - search for files in a directory hierarchy[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[m[m
       [1mfind[m [-H] [-L] [-P] [-D debugopts] [-Olevel] [starting-point...] [expression][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[m[m
       This  manual page documents the GNU version of [1mfind[m.  GNU [1mfind[m searches the directo
ry tree[m
[7m--More--[27m       rooted at each given starting-point by evaluating the given expression from left to right,[m
       according  to  the rules of precedence (see section OPERATORS), until the outcome is known[m
       (the left hand side is false for [4mand[24m operations, true for [4mor[24m), at which point  
[1mfind[m  moves[m
       on to the next file name.  If no starting-point is specified, `.' is assumed.[m
[m
       If  you  are  using [1mfind[m in an environment where security is important (for example if y
ou[m
       are using it to search directories that are writable by other users), you should read  the[m
       `Security  Considerations' chapter of the findutils documentation, which is called [1mFinding
[m[m
       [1mFiles[m and comes with findutils.   That document also includes a lot more detail  and  di
sโ[m
       cussion than this manual page, so you may find it a more useful source of information.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[m[m
       The [1m-H[m, [1m-L[m and [1m-P[m options control the treatment of symbolic links.  Command-li
ne arguments[m
       following these are taken to be names of files or directories to be examined,  up  to  the[m
       first  argument  that  begins with `-', or the argument `(' or `!'.  That argument and any[m
       following arguments are taken to be the expression describing what is to be searched  for.[m
       If  no  paths  are  given,  the current directory is used.  If no expression is given, the[m
       expression [1m-print[m is used (but you should probably consider using  [1m-print0[m  instead
,  anyโ[m
       way).[m
[m
       This  manual page talks about `options' within the expression list.  These options control[m
       the behaviour of [1mfind[m but are specified immediately after the last path  name.   The  fi
ve[m
       `real' options [1m-H[m, [1m-L[m, [1m-P[m, [1m-D[m and [1m-O[m must appear before the first pa
th name, if at all.  A[m
       double dash [1m--[m can also be used to signal that any remaining  arguments  are  not  optio
ns[m
       (though ensuring that all start points begin with either `./' or `/' is generally safer if[m
       you use wildcards in the list of start points).[m
